Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnea (OSA) is a breathing disorder characterized by frequent interruptions of breathing during sleep due to the blockage of air flow in the upper airways.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma and dentigerous cysts are oral conditions that affect the teeth and surrounding structures.
  Orbital fracture is a break in the bones around the eye and is not typically associated with sleep apnea.
  Temporomandibular joint (TMJ) ankylosis occurs when there is a bony or fibrous adhesion of the mandible to the skull, and it can lead to difficulty in opening the mouth.
  OSA can be caused by many physical factors, and TMJ ankylosis is one of them.
  Therefore, the correct answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: Obstructive sleep apnoea (OSA) occurs due to obstruction of airflow during sleep. This obstruction of airflow can occur due to various reasons like swollen tonsils, obesity, large tongue, and jaw bone abnormalities. Among the given options, Mandibular ameloblastoma, Dentigerous cyst, and Orbital fracture are not known to cause obstruction of airflow during sleep leading to sleep apnea. On the other hand, Bilateral TMJ (Temporomandibular Joint) Ankylosis refers to the fusion of the jawbone, which can obstruct the airway and cause OSA. Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")

   An orbital fracture is an injury that occurs to the bony socket, and it may cause double vision and Inability to move the eye, but it's not related to OSA
  Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.

  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg

  The TG level for the patient is 276 mg/dL, which is also high.

  Both Rosuvastatin and Atorvastatin are used to lower the LDL levels.
  Since the LDL level of the patient is quite high, it is preferred to use Atorvastatin.

  In addition, the TG levels are elevated, which suggests the presence of mixed dyslipidemia.

Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Thought:
- The floor of the third ventricle is present in the brain.
- Optic stalks are located between the third ventricle and the optic vesicles in embryonic development. 
- The third nerve is a nerve that emerges from the brainstem and runs along the base of the brain, then through the cavernous sinus in the skull, before entering the orbit and supplying the muscles that move the eye.
- The infundibulum connects the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland.
- The mammillary bodies are located on the undersurface of the brain and are part of the limbic system.
- Therefore, the structure that is not present on floor of third ventricle is third nerve (B).

Topic: Microbiology
Question: For which of the following is PPV-23 is most beneficial:
Choices:
  A: Cystic fibrosis patient
  B: Sickle cell anemia patient
  C: Patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis
  D: Child less than 2 years
Response 0:
Thought:
PPV-23 is a pneumococcal polysaccharide vaccine used to protect against Streptococcus pneumoniae infections.
Streptococcus pneumoniae can cause pneumonia, meningitis and sepsis, among other diseases.
Cystic Fibrosis Patients have a weakened immune system and can benefit from the vaccine.
Sickle cell anemia patients are also susceptible to Streptococcus pneumoniae infections due to their weakened immune system.
Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis are not necessarily more susceptible to Streptococcus pneumoniae infections.
Children less than 2 years of age have a different vaccine regimen from PPV-23, which is given to people who are 65 years or older and those with certain medical conditions.
Therefore, the answer is A: Cystic fibrosis patient.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  PPV-23 is a vaccine that helps protect against 23 strains of pneumococcal bacteria.
  Cystic fibrosis is a genetic disorder causes lung infections, but the pneumococcal infections are not necessarily more common in cystic fibrosis patients.
  Sickle cell anemia is a blood disorder where the blood cells change shape and can get stuck in blood vessels, causing infections that PPV-23 doesn't necessarily protect against.
  PPV-23 is most beneficial for preventing pneumococcal infections in people with weakened immune systems, or chronic lung diseases, like recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  PPV-23 stands for pneumococcal polysaccharide vaccine and is administered to protect against pneumococcal disease.
  The vaccine may be given to individuals more vulnerable to infections such as those with certain health conditions.
  Cystic fibrosis, sickle cell anemia, and recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis are all conditions that can make the patient more susceptible to infections.
  Children less than 2 years old have a higher risk of getting pneumococcal disease than older children.
  However, the question is asking which patient is MOST BENEFITED by PPV-23 vaccine.
  According to CDC, adults (>=19) with the medical conditions such as the list shown in option C, or immunocompromised (including HIV), should receive the vaccine.
  Thus, the answer is C: Patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis.

  PPV-23 is Pneumococcal polysaccharide vaccine and is used to prevent pneumococcal disease caused by the bacterium Streptococcus pneumoniae.

Topic: Dental
Question: Mandibular Molar is
Choices:
  A: Tritubercular teeth
  B: Quadritubercular teeth
  C: Haplodont
  D: Triconodont
Response 0:
Thought:
  Mandibular molars are the molars located in the lower jaw.
  Tritubercular teeth have three main cusps or points.
  Quadritubercular teeth have four cusps or points.
  Haplodont teeth are simple, with one point or cusp.
  Triconodont teeth have three cusps arranged in a triangle shape.
  The mandibular molars are usually quadritubercular.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The Mandibular Molar is a type of tooth.
  In dentistry, the "mandibular" term relates to the lower arch of teeth.
  "Molar" is a type of tooth that is located in the back of the mouth, with a broad surface used for grinding food.
  Tritubercular teeth have three main cusps or tubercles in the crown.
  Quadritubercular teeth have four main cusps or tubercles in the crown.
  Haplodont teeth have a single cusp.
  Triconodont teeth have three cones formed on their cutting edge and are particularly useful in tearing down flesh and crushing bones.
  Since molars have multiple cusps or tubercles, options A, C, and D can be eliminated as they refer to types of teeth with fewer cusps or tubercles.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Quadritubercular teeth.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  There are four types of mammalian molars: Haplodont, Bunodont, Lophodont, and Selenodont.
  Mandibular molar refers to the molars that exist in the lower jaw.
  Tritubercular and Quadritubercular molars have three and four cusps respectively and are found in primitive mammals.
  Triconodont molars have a single cusp and are also found in some primitive mammals. 
  The molars of most mammals including humans are either Haplodont, Bunodont, Lophodont, or Selenodont.
  Therefore, Mandibular Molar is not Tritubercular, Quadritubercular or Triconodont, but is Haplodont as it consists of a simple base and no additional structures like ridges or cusps.

  Typically, human mandibular molars have four cusps.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Quadritubercular teeth.

Topic: Surgery
Question: Which one of the following is a muscle splitting incision?
Choices:
  A: Kocher's incision
  B: Rutherford-Morrison incision
  C: Pfannenstiel incision
  D: Lanz incision
Response 0:
Thought: 
  A muscle splitting incision is an incision that is made through the muscle fibers instead of dividing them.
  Pfannenstiel incision is located in the lower abdomen and typically is used for surgeries in the pelvis and lower abdomen, such as C-sections and hysterectomies.
  Rutherford-Morrison incision is a curved incision over the flank.
  Lanz incision is a muscle splitting incision used for surgeries such as appendectomies and upper abdominal surgeries.
  Kocher's incision is a muscle-cutting incision that is used to access the hip joint or the upper end of the femur.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Lanz incision.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  A muscle splitting incision is an incision which is made along, or parallel to, the muscle fibers.
  Kocher's incision is a type of straight incision, which is made vertically over the anterior right rectus sheath.
  Rutherford-Morrison incision is a type of oblique incision, and it is made along the right costal margin.
  Pfannenstiel incision is a transverse incision, located just above the pubic bone.
  Lanz incision is a type of muscle-splitting incision used to access the appendix, located between McBurney's point and the navel.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Lanz incision
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  A muscle splitting incision is used to access a deep organ while minimizing the damage to the muscle fibers.
  Lanz incision is a muscle-splitting incision made in the anterior abdominal wall, primarily for appendectomy.
  Kocher’s incision is made in upper abdomen, primarily for accessing the pancreas, and does not usually involve splitting any muscles.
  Pfannenstiel incision is a transverse incision in lower abdominal wall made above the pubic hairline, primarily for accessing the pelvic organs.
  Rutherford-Morrison incision is an oblique incision made in the right iliac fossa, primarily for accessing the appendix.
  Therefore, Lanz incision is a muscle splitting incision.

Thought: 
Muscle splitting incisions refer to incisions made by splitting the muscle fibers and not cutting through them to access the underlying tissue or organ. 
Kocher's Incision is a subcostal muscle-splitting incision that is used to access the gallbladder, bile ducts, and proximal duodenum.
Rutherford-Morrison incision is not a muscle-splitting incision.
Pfannenstiel incision is a transverse muscle-cutting lower abdominal incision that is used for gynecologic or lower intestinal surgeries.
Lanz incision is a muscle-cutting incision used in the right lower abdomen for appendectomy surgery.
Therefore, the answer is A: Kocher's incision.

  A Lanz incision is a transverse incision made on the right side of the abdomen, usually for surgeries involving the appendix.
  A Rutherford-Morrison incision is a type of flank incision usually used to reach the kidney or to be used during a nephrectomy.
  A muscle splitting incision is performed by dividing the fibers of the muscle and not cutting through the muscle itself. The technique is common in orthopedic and spine surgeries.
  Therefore, the correct answer is D: Lanz incision since it involves dividing the fibers of the abdominal muscles, instead of cutting through them.

  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that appear in young children.
  Primary teeth have thinner dentine and enamel layers than permanent teeth.
  Pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in primary teeth because:
  1. Increased odontoblastic activity in the young:
     Odontoblasts are cells that form a layer adjacent to the pulp tissue in teeth.
     They are responsible for producing dentine in response to injury or damage to the pulp.
     In young teeth, these cells are more active, and dentine is produced more rapidly.
     Therefore, during a pulpectomy, it is easier to remove infected pulp without causing injury to the tooth's structure.
  2. Increased blood supply through the wide apex:
     Primary teeth have wider and shorter roots than permanent teeth.
     The short length of the root forms a wide opening at the apex (the tip of the root where the blood vessels enter and exit).
     The increased blood supply makes it easier to promote healing and repair after the procedures.
  3. Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young:
     Collagen fibres are the structural protein fibres present in tissues such as skin, bone, and cartilage.
     In young teeth, there is a lesser amount of collagen fibres.
     This makes it easier to place fillings, sealants, and other dental restorations.
     
  Therefore, the answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.

Question: Arrange the sequence of auditory pathway from peripheral to central: Inferior colliculus Cochlear nucleus Auditory coex Medial geniculate body
Choices:
  A: B>A>D>C
  B: B>D>C>A
  C: A>D>B>C
  D: C>A>B>D
Response 0:
Thought:
  The auditory pathway starts from the peripheral ear and ends up in the central nervous system.
  Cochlea is the peripheral ear receptor for sound.
  The first central station in the auditory pathway is the Cochlear nucleus.
  Inferior colliculus and medial geniculate body are intermediate stations.
  Auditory cortex is the final station in the auditory pathway.
  Therefore, the correct sequence of the auditory pathway from peripheral to central is B: B>D>C>A, where B is Cochlear nucleus, D is Inferior colliculus, C is Auditory cortex, and A is Medial geniculate body.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The auditory pathway describes the structure that sound waves follow from the ear to the brain. 
  Soundwaves enter the ear, then pass through the auditory canal and vibrate the tympanic membrane or eardrum.
  The vibrations are then transmitted through the three tiny bones of the ear - the malleus, incus, and stapes - which amplify and carry the vibrations to the inner ear.
  In the inner ear, the vibrations are transformed into electrical signals by the cochlear hair cells
  The auditory pathway is divided into peripheral, brainstem, and central components.
  From the question, the sequence is from peripheral to central. 
  So, the arrangement should show the order from how the auditory signal enters (peripheral) up to where it goes in the brain (central).
  The auditory signal follows this pathway: Cochlear nucleus, Superior olivary nucleus, Inferior colliculus, Medial geniculate body. 
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  The auditory pathway starts from the cochlea in the peripheral and ends in the central auditory cortex.
  The cochlear nerve fibers synapse at the cochlear nucleus, then information travels to the superior olivary complex, the lateral lemniscus, and the inferior colliculus, respectively.
  After processing in the inferior colliculus, the information is transferred to the medial geniculate body in the thalamus.
  From the thalamus, information is then conveyed to the auditory cortex in the temporal lobe.
  Therefore, the correct sequence is from the Cochlear nucleus to the Inferior colliculus to the Medial geniculate body to the Auditory cortex.
  The answer is C: A>D>B>C.

Topic: Dental
Question: Working cusps are also known as:
Choices:
  A: Guiding cusps.
  B: Supporting cusps.
  C: Holding cusps.
  D: Balancing cusps.
Response 0:
Thought: 
  A cusp is a pointed or rounded eminence on or near the masticating surface of a tooth.
  Working cusps are those that contact the opposing teeth during the chewing or grinding of food.
  This cusp influences the direction of movement of the lower jaw.
  Guiding cusps are responsible for guiding the lower jaw in a forward-backward position.
  Therefore, working cusps can also be known as Guiding cusps.
  The answer is A: Guiding cusps.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
Working cusps are those that are actively involved in the masticatory movements.
The forces are transmitted by these cusps during mandibular movements.
Guiding, holding and balancing cusps are not the same as Working cusps.
Supporting cusps may bear a load but they are not involved in active masticatory movements.
Therefore, the correct answer is B: Supporting cusps.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
Working cusps are those that are involved in the chewing (or cutting) of food.
Guiding cusps are those that guide the mandible (lower jaw) in its movements.
Supporting cusps are those that help bear a load or pressure.
Holding cusps is not a commonly used term in dentistry.
Balancing cusps are the cusps that contact each other on the non-working side of the arch (the side that is not chewing).
Therefore, the answer is A: Guiding cusps.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Thought:
  Cusps are the raised points on the chewing surface of the teeth.
  Working cusps are those on the mandibular (lower) posterior teeth that come into contact with the maxillary (upper) posterior teeth when a person chews food in a side-to-side or lateral movement.
  Guiding cusps are on the maxillary posterior teeth that guide (or control) the movement of the mandibular posterior teeth during lateral movements.
  Supporting cusps are also referred to as non-working cusps, as they do not contact opposing teeth during chewing.
  Holding cusps is not a commonly used term in dentistry that relates to cuspal anatomy.
  Balancing cusps are found on maxillary posterior teeth and balance the chewing forces generated by the working cusps to create efficient chewing.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Guiding cusps.

  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres

  Normally, the PDL fibres are attached to cementum.
  If PDL fibres lose their attachment to cementum, they can attach to dentin and form new attachment.
  Co-adaptation is a natural mechanism that involves changes in the position and orientation of tooth.

VLDL is denser than chylomicrons because they are smaller; and, therefore, have less fat content.

  They differ in their lipid and protein composition.
  The density of the different lipoproteins depends on their composition.
  Chylomicrons are the largest and the least dense of all lipoproteins, and they transport predominantly dietary triglycerides.

  LDL (Low Density Lipoprotein) is also synthesized by the liver and carries cholesterol from the liver to the peripheral tissues.
  HDL (High Density Lipoprotein), another product of the liver, collects excess cholesterol from peripheral tissues and sends it back to the liver. 
  HDL carries more protein and less lipid and thus is the densest lipoprotein among the four.
  Therefore, the option having the least density is the one that carries more fat and less protein.
  The answer is D: Chylomicrons.

Question: Occurrence of malocclusion in given population is best described as:

  A: Prevalence rate
  B: Incidence rate

  D: Probability
Response 0:
Thought:
Malocclusion is a permanent or semi-permanent misalignment of teeth.
Prevalence rate is the proportion of individuals in a population having a specific disease or condition over a specified period of time.
Incidence rate is the number of new cases of a disease or condition within a specific time period in a given population.
Morbidity refers to the state of having a disease or medical condition.
Probability is a statistical term that refers to the chance of occurrence of an event or outcome.
Since the question asks about the overall proportion of individuals in a population who have malocclusion, the appropriate term would be prevalence rate. Therefore, the answer is A: Prevalence rate.

  A: DMT-1
  B: Ferropoin
  C: Transferrin
  D: Hepcidin

  Ferropoin is not related to iron in enterocytes.
  Transferrin is an iron-transporting protein in the blood, not related to iron uptake by enterocytes.
  Hepcidin is a hormone responsible for regulating iron homeostasis.

  Transferrin is the protein that carries Iron in the bloodstream and does not involve the transport of Iron into enterocytes.

Response 1:
Thought:
  RPD stands for Removable Partial Denture.
  Looseness in RPD may be due to incorrect fitting of the components.
  Occlusal Balancing relates to the adjustment of the occlusion in natural teeth.
  Passive clasp does not cause looseness.
  Thin flange or less coverage may have an impact on retention but doesn't cause looseness.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  RPD refers to Removable Partial Denture.
  The looseness seen in a recently delivered RPD could be due to one of the following factors:
    - Defective occlusal balancing: This refers to any imbalances in the way the upper and lower teeth come together when the patient bites down. This can cause the RPD to rock and move around.
    - Passive clasp on abutment: A clasp is used to keep the RPD in place but if it is too passive, it will not grip the abutment tightly enough to keep the RPD secure.
    - Thin flange: The flange is the part of the RPD that extends away from the teeth and holds the denture in place. If the flange is too thin it will not hold the RPD securely.
    - Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth: If there is not enough overlap between the posterior teeth, the RPD may not be anchored to the teeth properly.
  Out of all these choices, the most probable cause of looseness seen in a recently delivered RPD could be due to Passive clasp on abutment.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Passive clasp on abutment.

Response 4:
Thought: 
Looseness of any dental prosthesis needs to be evaluated by examining the possible causes.
RPD stands for Removable Partial Denture.
Occlusal balancing ensures that the upper and lower teeth meet evenly and disperse the biting force appropriately. If the occlusion is poorly adjusted, the biting pressure may not be distributed evenly, leading to loosening of the prosthesis.
Clasps are used to secure a prosthesis to abutment. If the clasp passively engages the abutment, it may lead to some degree of looseness.
Flange is the part of the prosthesis that rests on the gingiva. If the flange is thin, it may not be able to provide enough support to keep the prosthesis stable.
Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth means that the occlusal surface of the posterior teeth on the prosthesis does not adequately land on the opposing teeth when the mouth is closed.
Looseness in a recently delivered RPD can be due to several reasons, but passive clasp on abutment seems to be the most common cause.
Therefore, the answer is B: Passive clasp on abutment.

  The abscess needs to be drained, thus treatment of choice will be incision & drainage with antibiotics cover.
  Hence, the answer is A: Incision & drainage.

  A: Glycolysis
  B: Glycogenolysis
  C: TCA cycle
  D: Phosphocreatine
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The question is asking for a rapid source of energy for exercising muscles by resynthesizing ATP.
  Glycolysis is the metabolic process that breaks down glucose to produce ATP, but it is not as rapid as some other mechanisms.
  Glycogenolysis is the breakdown of glycogen to produce glucose, which can then be used in glycolysis. However, it is not the most rapid energy source.
  The TCA cycle is a metabolic pathway that produces ATP, but it is not as rapid as the other options.
  Phosphocreatine is a high-energy molecule that can rapidly donate a phosphate group to ADP to resynthesize ATP. Therefore, it is a rapid source of energy for exercising muscles.
  The answer is D: Phosphocreatine.

  Glycogenolysis is the breakdown of glycogen to glucose in the liver and muscles to be used as a primary energy source during exercise.
  TCA cycle occurs in the mitochondria as a sequence of biochemical reactions converting acetyl CoA to CO2 and H2O to release energy stored in the chemical bonds.
  Phosphocreatine is an energy-rich compound of the muscles and is used during the initial seconds of intense exercise for the rapid resynthesis of ATP.
  Therefore, the correct answer is D: Phosphocreatine.

Question: Alginate fillers derived from
Choices:
  A: Calcium sulphate
  B: Sodium phosphate
  C: Potassium alginate
  D: Diatomaceous earth
Response 0:
Action: Answer("C")

  Alginate fillers are used to make impressions of teeth in dentistry.
  Alginate is a linear, anionic polysaccharide, which is derived from brown seaweeds.
  The chemical formula of alginate is (C6H7O6COO-)n.
  Alginate is capable of reacting with divalent cations, such as calcium ions, to form a gel.
  One commonly used alginate filler in dentistry is potassium alginate, which reacts with calcium ions from calcium sulphate that is also present in the mixture to form a gel. 
  Therefore, the answer is C: Potassium alginate.

These drugs have been studied in patients with impaired kidney function and no dose adjustment is required even in severe renal disease (3, 4).
  Repaglinide is an oral insulin secretagogue, which stimulates insulin production from the pancreas. It is rapidly metabolized in the liver and excreted in the bile. In patients with mild-to-moderate renal impairment, the recommended starting dose is 0.5 mg before meals. Avoid use in patients with severe renal impairment (creatinine clearance <20 mL/min). Dosage adjustment is not required in hepatic impairment (5).
  Glimepiride is another oral sulfonylurea that works by increasing insulin secretion from beta cells, stimulating insulin release from Pancreas. It is metabolized primarily in the liver and excreted in the urine. In patients with moderate to severe renal impairment (creatinine clearance <50 mL/min), the initial dose of glimepiride should be 1 mg daily (6, 7).
  
Conclusion:
  Vildagliptin and Linagliptin are two good choices as a hypoglycemic agent in the given patient, as both these drugs won't require renal dose modification. 
Action: Answer("A")
Response 8:

  Repaglinide is a non-sulfonylurea insulin secretagogue. It has no active metabolites and 90% of the drug is excreted in the bile. It has an advantage over sulfonylureas in that it is less likely to cause hypoglycemia, and doesn't accumulate with continuous use.
  Linagliptin is a Dipeptidyl Peptidase-4 (DPP-4) inhibitor. It's excreted primarily by the liver without any major renal elimination. It does not require any dose adjustment in renal failure.
  Vildagliptin is another DPP-4 inhibitor, which is excreted in the urine mainly as unchanged drug and doesn't require any dose adjustment, but it is not available in the United States.
  Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea agent that is metabolized in the liver and excreted by the kidneys. Suggested dose adjustments in moderate to severe renal impairment by some sources and should be used with caution in patients with renal impairment.
  The patient doesn't want to use injectable insulin. To management Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus in a 70 years old man with a history of hypertension and advanced CKD where one oral hypoglycemic agent can be used that doesn't require any renal dose modification, linagliptin would be preferred in this patient.

  Basal cell carcinoma is the most common type of skin cancer and is slow-growing.
  Fibrosarcoma is a type of malignant tumor that originates in the fibrous connective tissue of the body.
  Leukoplakia is a condition that causes white patches on the mucous membranes. It is not a carcinoma.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Basal cell carcinoma.
Action: Answer("B")

Question: Which of the following is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results?
Choices:
  A: Systematic random sampling
  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Thought:
    To select patients with respect to potential factors that may affect the result, we need to identify the potential factors and make sure that we have representation from each factors in the sample selected.
    Systematic random sampling is mainly used when there is a list of subjects available where the sampling unit is pre-determined and is available in a sequence.
    Simple random Sampling is drawing the study population from the available participants at random so every individual has an equal chance of being chosen for the study. 
    Stratified Random Sampling is used when the population is divided into smaller groups with similar characteristics and the sample is chosen from each group.
    Cluster Sampling is used when the population is divided into clusters (geographically defined or based on an observable grouping) and random clusters are selected for the study.
    Since Stratified Random Sampling divides the population into smaller groups and aims to select sample from each group, it is best suited to select patients with respect to potential factors that may affect the result.
    
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
- Systematic random sampling is a type of probability sampling in which every nth element is selected from a list or population.
- Simple random sampling is a type of probability sampling where every member of a population has an equal chance of being selected.
- Stratified random sampling is a sampling technique in which the population is divided into strata or sub-groups, and random samples are taken from each stratum.
- Cluster sampling is a sampling technique where groups or clusters of individuals are selected randomly instead of individuals.
- The question is asking about selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
- In that case, Stratified random sampling, where the population is divided into subgroups based on those potential factors, and random samples are chosen from each subgroup, would be the most appropriate method.
- Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.

- Selecting participants based on potential factors that will affect the results means selecting a representative sample based on some characteristic(s).
- Stratified random sampling ensures the sample is representative of each stratum.

Topic: Dental
Question: Which of the following has strong familial inheritance:

  B: Class I type I
  C: Class II div I
  D: Class II div II
Response 0:
Thought: 
  For functional occlusion, there are three classes based on Angle's classification: Class I, Class II, and Class III.
  Class I refers to the normal occlusion. It is the union of the crowns of the teeth positioned in the right places and with the correct inclination.
  Both Class II and Class III are defined in terms of their anteroposterior relations between the maxilla and the mandible, and identify an overbite or underbite, respectively.
  Divisions of Class II in subcategories I or II are based on the position and inclination of upper incisors.
  There is strong familial inheritance between first-degree relatives for Class II div I.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Class II div I.

Thought: 
  Functional classes are determined by considering the relative positions of maxillary and mandibular first molars, along with the intermaxillary relation.
  Malocclusion is the positional imperfection of the teeth when jaws are closed.
  Malocclusion can be of any class (Class I, Class II, and Class III).
  Class I malocclusion is where the first molars are properly aligned, but there's overcrowding, spacing, overbite, or crossbite elsewhere.
  Class II malocclusion is one in which the lower first molar is posterior (further towards the back of the mouth) to the upper first molar. It is commonly referred to as retruded jaw or overjet.
  Class III malocclusion is when the lower first molar is anterior (further towards the front of the mouth) to the upper first molar. It is commonly referred to as protruded jaw or underjet. 
  Familial inheritance means that a certain trait is passed down through generations in a family. 
  According to studies, Class III malocclusion has strong familial inheritance.

  Non-depolarizing muscle relaxants block the acetylcholine receptors leading to muscle relaxation and paralysis.
  Short-acting non-depolarising muscle relaxants include mivacurium and atracurium.
  Succinylcholine is a short-acting depolarizing muscle relaxant.
  Pancuronium and Decamethonium are long-acting non-depolarising muscle relaxants.

  Succinylcholine is a depolarizing muscle relaxant and has a short duration of action making it not a non-depolarizing muscle relaxant.
  Pancuronium is a long-acting non-depolarizing muscle relaxant, so it cannot be the correct answer.
  Mivacurium is a short-acting non-depolarizing muscle relaxant used for rapid sequence intubation and muscle relaxation during surgery, then it is a possible answer.
  Decamethonium is an ultra short-acting non-depolarizing muscle relaxant that has been largely abandoned due to its side-effect profile.
